<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto"><i>Xscape</i> (album)</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p><i><b>Xscape</b></i> is the second <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Special:Search/posthumous" title="wikt:Special:Search/posthumous">posthumous</a> album<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> of previously unreleased tracks by American singer <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>. It was released on May 13, 2014 by <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/MJJ_Music" title="MJJ Music">MJJ Music</a>. It is the eleventh album released by Sony and Motown since <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Michael_Jackson" title="Death of Michael Jackson">Jackson's death</a> in June 2009. <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a>, chairman of Epic Records, <a href="/wiki/Curator" title="Curator">curated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executively produced</a> the album enlisting <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> to lead a team of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_producers" title="Record producers">record producers</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" title="Stargate (production team)">StarGate</a>, <a href="/wiki/J-Roc_(record_producer)" title="J-Roc (record producer)">Jerome "J-Roc" Harmon</a>, John McClain, and <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Rodney Jerkins</a>, to retool and contemporize the eight selected tracks. Jerkins produced the title song and is the only original song producer to work on the final productions.</p>
<p><i>Xscape</i> was promoted across the Sony group of companies; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Mobile" title="Sony Mobile">Sony Mobile</a> used a snippet of "<a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a>" in their advertising campaign for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xperia_Z2" title="Xperia Z2">Xperia Z2</a> mobile phone. Early reviews have been mixed to positive. "<a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a>" was announced as the official lead single to premiere on May 1, 2014. The deluxe edition of the album includes all of the songs in their original forms as well as one bonus track and two videos.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xscape_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Officially announced on March 31, 2014, <i>Xscape</i> features 8 tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialannouncement_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-officialannouncement-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> It is the second such album of posthumous material to be released by Epic Records since Jackson's death in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The title track "Xscape" was recorded in 2001 for Jackson's tenth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Invincible_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Invincible (Michael Jackson album)">Invincible</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> American producer <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a> executively produced the album, with addition production from <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins" title="Rodney Jerkins">Rodney Jerkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" title="Stargate (production team)">StarGate</a> and John McClain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timenews_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-timenews-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Timbaland said that Reid had personally approached the producer at his home to discuss the new Jackson project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Timbo_Interview_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Timbo_Interview-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Johnson_(musician)" title="Jesse Johnson (musician)">Jesse Johnson</a>, former lead guitarist of the American band <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Time_(band)" title="The Time (band)">The Time</a> revealed that he had worked on elements of one song that featured <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Questlove" title="Questlove">Questlove</a>, and <a href="/wiki/D%27Angelo" title="D'Angelo">D'Angelo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the track failed to be included in the final track listing of the album. Reid said that they wanted to honor Jackson's legacy when naming the album, "the title of this album (<i>Xscape</i>) honors Michael's album naming process. He always chose a song from the album to name his projects and, beginning with <i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i>, used only one word titles, each with an edgy quality to them (<i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_(album)" title="Bad (album)">Bad</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Dangerous (Michael Jackson album)">Dangerous</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/HIStory:_Past,_Present_and_Future,_Book_I" title="HIStory: Past, Present and Future, Book I">HIStory</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Invincible_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Invincible (Michael Jackson album)">Invincible</a></i>). This is true of the new project."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Press_Release_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Press_Release-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_history">Recording history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xscape_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a>" was co-written by Canadian singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Paul_Anka" title="Paul Anka">Paul Anka</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corner_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corner-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and originally recorded in 1983 as a demo with Anka at the piano. The song was also recorded by American entertainer <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mathis" title="Johnny Mathis">Johnny Mathis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Showbiz411.com_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Showbiz411.com-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> A duet version of the song with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> was recorded and released as a single - the song featured percussion and breaths from Jackson's 1979 song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Workin%27_Day_And_Night" title="Workin' Day And Night">Workin' Day And Night</a>".</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Chicago_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Chicago (Michael Jackson song)">Chicago</a>" (originally called "She Was Lovin' Me") was recorded in 1999 but failed to make the <i><a href="/wiki/Invincible_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Invincible (Michael Jackson album)">Invincible</a></i> album.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Loving_You_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Loving You (Michael Jackson song)">Loving You</a>" was recorded between 1985 and 1987 during the "<a href="/wiki/Bad_(album)" title="Bad (album)">Bad</a>" sessions.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/A_Place_with_No_Name" title="A Place with No Name">A Place With No Name</a>" was written and recorded in 1998. The track resembles "<a href="/wiki/A_Horse_with_No_Name" title="A Horse with No Name">A Horse with No Name</a>," a hit song by American rock band <a href="/wiki/America_(band)" title="America (band)">America</a>. A 24-second snippet was leaked online by <a href="/wiki/TMZ" title="TMZ">TMZ</a> in July 2009 and a full version was leaked in December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a>" was recorded during the <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Dangerous (Michael Jackson album)">Dangerous</a></i> sessions in 1991. A Tricky Stewart remix version leaked on the internet in 2010, which was intended for the first posthumous album, <i><a href="/wiki/Michael_(album)" title="Michael (album)">Michael</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a> also recorded a "duet version" featured with Jackson's vocals, which was leaked in August 2013. The Michael Jackson Estate afterwards stated that they had not authorized the release of this recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Do You Know Where Your Children Are" was written and recorded in 1990 during the <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Dangerous (Michael Jackson album)">Dangerous</a></i> sessions, but did not make the cut.</p>
<p>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Gangsta_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Blue Gangsta (Michael Jackson song)">Blue Gangsta</a>" was written and recorded in 1998 but failed to make the <i>Invincible</i> album. Rapper Tempamental remixed the song without Jackson's permission and made it available on his MySpace web page in late 2006. The remix titled "Gangsta (No Friend of Mine)" featured <a href="/wiki/Pras" title="Pras">Pras</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Fugees" title="Fugees">Fugees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"Xscape" was written and recorded in 1999 during his <i>Invincible</i> album recording sessions but failed to make the album. The song was completed in 2001 and leaked on the internet the following year. The tune has been given a modern spin by its original producer, Rodney Jerkins, and features samples of "<a href="/wiki/You_Rock_My_World" title="You Rock My World">You Rock My World</a>", a song recorded in the same era as "Xscape".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion_and_singles">Promotion and singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xscape_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Promotion and singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Two official singles <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Place_With_No_Name" title="A Place With No Name">A Place With No Name</a></i> were released from <i>Xscape</i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a></i> was the first song announced for the album, and appeared on several notable music charts due to digital downloads and streaming. <i><a href="/wiki/Loving_You_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Loving You (Michael Jackson song)">Loving You</a></i> was released as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promotional_single" title="Promotional single">promotional single</a> at UK radios.</p>
<p>In February 2014, Sony and Jackson's estate announced a partnership with Sony Mobile that saw the release of an ad incorporating a new version of the track "<a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a>", which has been confirmed as one of the album tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbnews1_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbnews1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The commercial advertisement was for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Mobile" title="Sony Mobile">Sony Mobile</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xperia_Z2" title="Xperia Z2">Xperia Z2</a> mobile phone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The album had been aired to the UK media in the basement of a <a href="/wiki/Knightsbridge" title="Knightsbridge">Knightsbridge</a> hotel on March 31, 2014. The journalists were permitted to hear the album once without any electronic devices, and song titles were kept secret.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-standardeve_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-standardeve-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The entertainment correspondents for some UK media, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skynews_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-skynews-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/London_Evening_Standard" title="London Evening Standard">London Evening Standard</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-standardeve_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-standardeve-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-tele-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Mixmag" title="Mixmag">Mixmag</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mixmag_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mixmag-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DigitalSpy_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-DigitalSpy-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> were invited.</p>
<p>On April 30, it was revealed that "<a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a>" would be unveiled at the <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio" title="IHeartRadio">iHeartRadio</a> Music Awards on May 1 as the album's first single, contradicting statements by Timbaland that suggested that "Chicago" would be released first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_Timbo_Interview_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Timbo_Interview-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> It was co-written by Canadian singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Paul_Anka" title="Paul Anka">Paul Anka</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corner_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corner-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> and features <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> "Love Never Felt So Good" was previously recorded by American entertainer <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mathis" title="Johnny Mathis">Johnny Mathis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Showbiz411.com_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Showbiz411.com-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The digital download for the single became available on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> at 0:01 <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a> on May 2, 2014 for the album version and the duet version with <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The release date of the single to urban radio stations confirmed as May 6, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debutsingledate_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-debutsingledate-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On May 4, the track "<a href="/wiki/Chicago_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Chicago (Michael Jackson song)">Chicago</a>" became available to <a href="/wiki/Music_Unlimited" title="Music Unlimited">Music Unlimited</a> subscribers, being followed by "Loving You", "<a href="/wiki/A_Place_with_No_Name" title="A Place with No Name">A Place with No Name</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a>", and "Do You Know Where Your Children Are" in the succeeding days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Pepper%27s_ghost" title="Pepper's ghost">Pepper's ghost</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> illusion of Michael Jackson performed "Slave to the Rhythm,” at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2014 Billboard Music Awards">2014 Billboard Music Awards</a> on May 18, 2014. The performance was choreographed by the Talauega brothers and was directed by Jamie King.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> A day after the coverage, the live performance of Slave to the Rhythm was uploaded to Michael Jackson's VEVO YouTube Channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following the success of "<a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a>" on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, Jackson became the first solo artist to have a single reach the top 10 in five different decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Slave_to_the_Rhythm_(Michael_Jackson_song)" title="Slave to the Rhythm (Michael Jackson song)">Slave to the Rhythm</a>", which debuted at number 45 on the Billboard charts, was Jackson's 50th Hot 100 hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xscape_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i></td>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle">B<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Entertainment_Weekly_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Entertainment_Weekly-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></td>

</table>
<p><i>Xscape</i> has a score of 66 out of 100 on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, based on 22 critics, indicating generally favorable reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to the album release, <i>Xscape</i> was played for critics at exclusive album listening parties in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Bernadette McNulty from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> praised the album as "pristine", noting the "front-and-center presence of Jackson's voice in the mix".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tele_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-tele-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Michael Cragg from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> said <i>Xscape</i> feels "like an album created to showcase a handful of Jackson songs that on the whole deserve to be heard".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Richard Suchet from <i><a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a></i> thought the album "sound[ed] more like modern-day remixes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skynews_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-skynews-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Nick Stevenson from <i><a href="/wiki/Mixmag" title="Mixmag">Mixmag</a></i> asserted that the album was "more like a collection of B-sides from <i><a href="/wiki/Off_the_Wall_(album)" title="Off the Wall (album)">Off the Wall</a></i> than a follow-up to <i><a href="/wiki/Invincible_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Invincible (Michael Jackson album)">Invincible</a></i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mixmag_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mixmag-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Michael Arceneaux from <i><a href="/wiki/Ebony_(magazine)" title="Ebony (magazine)">Ebony</a></i> said "the upcoming project 'from' the late singer sounds like a recipe for legacy tarnishing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ebonyreview_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ebonyreview-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Elysa Gardner of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> said that the producers on the album "ensure that Jackson's enduring strengths as a singer are represented, layering in modern electronic textures without overwhelming the distinctly slinky, shivery vocals or overall structure of the tunes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA_Today_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-USA_Today-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Other critics suggested the product was just a way to promote Sony smartphones,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> and had questions about the songwriting and production,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> or with the singing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Self-confessed Jackson-fan Nekesa Mumbi Moody, writing for Yahoo, said that much of the album had a dated feel, with "A Place With No Name" having poor lyrics and sound. She concluded that "putting out music that falls below Jackson's standards detracts from the carefully constructed catalog he spent decades creating and protecting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Xscape_(album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Xscape</i> became Jackson's tenth UK number-one album after it debuted atop the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> with 47,764 first-week sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, sales of the album in the UK stand at 135,500 copies and has been certified gold by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>. The album also debuted at number one in Belgium, Denmark, France, and Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> It debuted at number two on the US Billboard charts with first-week sales of 157,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In its second week of sales, the album sold 67,000 more copies. In its third week it sold 35,000 copies bringing its total sales to 259,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> In its fourth week, it sold a little more than 25,000 copies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> and the fifth week it sold a little less than 25,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5thweeksale_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-5thweeksale-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The album has sold 459,000 copies in the US as of January 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Canada, the album debuted at number three on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, selling 12,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<td style="padding-right: 10px; text-align: right; vertical-align: top;">1.</td>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">"<a href="/wiki/Love_Never_Felt_So_Good" title="Love Never Felt So Good">Love Never Felt So Good</a>"  </td>
<td style="vertical-align: top;">
<div class="hlist">
